ARIE 1919-1920 [vol. 042]


A.--List of copper-plates examined during the year 1919-20.


ARIE/1919-1920/A/1919-20/1 (page 11)
Placement
Mr. Raghavayya, trustee of the Kālahasti and Guḍi-mallam temples, Chittoor dis-trict.
Dynasty
Bāṇa
King
Vikramāditya
Date
…
Language
Sanskrit in Grantha & Tamil
Origin
Under corres-pondence for purchase.
Edition
…
Remarks
Gives a genealogy for five generations from Nandivarman. Records the gift of the village of Viprapīṭha free of all taxes to a number of Brahmans.
ARIE/1919-1920/A/1919-20/2 (page 11)
Placement
The Tahsildar of Nellore
Dynasty
…
King
Mahārāja Damōdaravarman of Ānanda-gōtra.
Date
[2]nd year, Kārttika, śu. di., trayōdaśī.
Language
Sanskrit in Telugu
Origin
Under corres-pondence for purchase.
Edition
…
Remarks
Gift of the village of Kaṅgūra free of all taxes to Brahmans of various gōtras. The king calls himself a devotee of Buddha. The grant was issued from Vijaya-Kandara-pura.
ARIE/1919-1920/A/1919-20/3 (page 11)
Placement
The Raja of Urlam through Mr. K.Nagesvara Rao Pantulu, Editor, ‘The An-dhra Patrika’, Madras.
Dynasty
Eastern Gaṅga.
King
Mahārāja Hastivarman
Date
80th year, Kārttika, ba. 8.
Language
Sanskrit in Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Registers the gift of 2(1/2) hala of land which was purchased from the residents of the agrahārika village of Hoṇḍēvaka in Krōsh-ṭuka-vartanī as an agrahāra to Jayaśarman of Vatsa-gōtra, a resident of Urāmalla (i.e., the modern Urlam). The king is called Rājasiṅgha and Raṇabhīta.
ARIE/1919-1920/A/1919-20/4 (page 11)

Mr. Subbayyar, truatee of the Vaidyanātha temple at Tirumaḻavāḍi, Trichinopoly district.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date

Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition

Remarks
Records a gift of land in the village of Gaṇḍarādittaṉ for conducting various ser-vices, for lamps and flower-gardens, to the temple of Tirumaḻavaḍi-Nāyaṉār by Śukadēvayyaṉ.
ARIE/1919-1920/A/1919-20/5 (page 11)
Placement
The Karnam of Chīmakurti, Ongole taluk, Guntur district.
Dynasty
Reḍḍi
King
Vēmaya Reḍḍi
Date
Śaka 1257, Yuva, Kārt-tika, śu. di., 12, Thurs-day, Man-vādi.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Mutilated at the end. Registers gift of cer-tain lands in the villages of Chīmakurti, Bhīmēśvaram, Pulikoṇḍa, Mailavaram and Kumārapuri, to Chiṭṭamūri Timmana Bhaṭṭa. The village of Rāmatīrtham in the Ammanavabrōli-sīma in the Śrīśaila-Bhūmi was also given to the same individual as agrahāra.
ARIE/1919-1920/A/1919-20/6 (page 11)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Divi Hanumachar, Koḍi-Tāḍipaṟṟu, Tenali taluk, Guntur district, through Mr. A.Rangaswami Sarasvati.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Anna-Vēma
Date
Śaka 1296, Nabhasya, Bhādrapada, Pūrṇimā, Wednesday, Lunar eclipse.
Language
Sanskrit & Telugu in Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Gives the genealogy of the Reḍḍi kings up to Anna-Vēma. Records the grant of the village of Pacchani-Tāṇḍipaṟṟu by the king to the scholar Peddi who was “the crest jewel among astronomers”.
ARIE/1919-1920/A/1919-20/7 (page 12)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Divi Hanumachar, Koḍi-Tāḍipaṟṟu, Tenali taluk, Guntur district through Mr. A.Rangaswami Sarasvati.
Dynasty
Reḍḍi
King
Vēma, son of Kōmaṭi
Date
Śaka 1341, Vikārin, Mārgaśira, Dhanus.
Language
Sanskrit & Telugu in Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Registers the gift, by the king, of the village Rudravaram to a number of Brahmans. The last verse of the inscription says that Śrīnātha, the Vidyādhikāri of king Vēma composed the inscription which ends with the sign-manual of the king ‘Śrī Vīranārāyaṇasya’.
ARIE/1919-1920/A/1919-20/8 (page 12)

Sanskrit & Telugu in Telugu
Origin

Edition
…
Remarks
The last of a set of plates. The boundaries of the granted village are given in Telugu. Then follows a verse in Sanskrit which says that the king gave to his preceptor Śaṅkara the village called Pinapāḍu and that Śrī-nātha-Bhaṭṭāraka composed the inscription.
ARIE/1919-1920/A/1919-20/9 (page 12)

Origin
Returned to the owner.

…
Remarks
Damaged. Registers the grant, by the king, of the village Mṟōpaṟṟu in Chanū[ṟpa]lli-vishaya to a Brahman called Maṇḍaśarman of the Vatsa-gōtra who was a resident of (the village) Vanapaṟṟu and was well-versed in the Vēdas and the Vēdāṅgas. The donee is stated to have been attached to (bhakta) Maṅgi Yuvarāja.

B.--Stone inscriptions copied in 1919 (continued from last Annual Report).


ARIE/1919-1920/B/1919/343 (page 13)
Placement
On the east side of the ‘rock,’ Aruḷāḷa-Perumāḷ temple. Little Conjeeveram, Conjeeveram taluk, Chingleput district.
Dynasty
…
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Vijaya Gaṇḍagō-pāladēva.
Date
8th year, Dhanus, śu. di., daśamī, Sunday, Rēvatī.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of 33 cattle for a perpetual lamp by a native of Malai-maṇḍalam to the temple of Aruḷāḷa-Perumāḷ who was pleased to take his stand in Tiruvattiyūr. Mentions the liquid measure Ariyaṉṉavallāṉ-nāḻi.
ARIE/1919-1920/B/1919/344 (page 13)
Placement
On the same wall
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
[2]7th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of one-eighth perpetual lamp by Gollappūṇḍi Dēvi-Nā-yakkaṉ residing in Śirumaṉai in Pākka-nāḍu to the same temple. The trustees of the temple took charge of the lamp.

Language
Tamil
Remarks

ARIE/1919-1920/B/1919/370 (page 15)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Vīrapratāpa Kṛishṇadēva-Mahārāya
Date
Śaka 1433, Prajā-pati, Siṁha, śu. di., pañchamī, Thursday, Svātī.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of the village of Pūlambākkam in Vaḍap[ā]-nāḍu, a subdivision of Puttanūr-kōṭṭam, a district of Paḍaivīḍu-rājya in Jayaṅgoṇḍasōḻa-maṇḍalam, for celebrating the festival in the month of Āvaṉi, by Vyāsa-Tīrtha (a Mādh-vaguru), disciple of Brahmaṇya-Tīrtha. Vyāsa-Tīrtha seems to have got the village as a gift from Kṛishṇarāya and the festival was instituted in his name. Vyāsa-Tīrtha also made a gift of the serpent-vehicle to be carried in procession on the 4th day of all festivals.
ARIE/1919-1920/B/1919/371 (page 15)

[1]1th year, Dha-nus, ba. di., daśa-mi, Thursday, Viśākhā.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Damaged. Records a gift of land by a merchant of Dīna-chintāmaṇinallūr for the consecration and worship of the image of Bhikshāṭanadēva set up by his father who died before consecrating it.

Date
6th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Refers to the lamps given during the reigns of Rājēndra-Chōḷadēva and Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷadēva, ‘who abolished tolls.’ Seems to provide for maintaining the lamps given during the time of Periyadēvar Rājarājadēva, as the recipients of the sheep died and their assignees could not either be found out or were unable to maintain the lamps.

ARIE/1919-1920/C/1920/304 (page 76)
Placement
On two pillars to the south of the Āḻvār shrine behind the sanctum of Śrī-Rāmabhadra temple at Bhadrachalam, Bhadrachalam taluk, Godavari district.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1754, Nandana, Chaitra, śu. di., 9, Sunday.
Language
Telugu
Remarks
Registers that a certain Varada-Rāmadāsu of Kāñchī-nagara, who was an incarnation of Śrī-Rāmadāsugāru of the time of Tānīsha, came to Bhadrādri and spent his time there as a devotee. In course of time he miraculously became the administrator of the Hasanābādu-Paragaṇa (in His Exalted Highness the Nizam's State) in the time of Nawāb Nāsaruddaula and conferred a large part of the income of that Paragaṇa on the temple and the Brahmans who were connected with it. Numerous other details concerning the establishment, festivals, worship, oblations, etc., of the temple are also registered.
ARIE/1919-1920/C/1920/305 (page 76)
Placement
On a mutilated pillar lying near the mirror-chamber in the same tem-ple.

Date
Śaka 1546, Raktāk-shi, Phālguṇa, śu. di., 5, Thursday.
Language
Telugu
Remarks
Damaged. Records that a certain lady devotee of Raghunāyaka of Bhadrāchalam, the wife of Mutyam Akkamappa, a Padmanāyaka born in the Vipparla-gōtra caused the mukha-maṇḍapa and the prākāra to be built as her charity in the temple and gave the whole of the village of Guṇḍāla for providing festivals and servants. Another part of the inscription records that a daughter of Mutyāla Rāmakka, named Appalamma, built and consecrated the shrine of Nammāḻvār; and her daughter, a certain Akkam .... built the bhōga-maṇḍapa for Raghunāyaka.

Remarks
Records that the village-chāvaḍi (racchayillu), tanks, and temple are of (i.e., constructed by?) Gujapotheri. His elder son died in the battle of Niḍumrānu (the present Niḍumānūr near Ongole). The Raṭṭaḍi (i.e., the Reddi of Niḍumānūr ?) gave two kaṇḍuga of field land ? (ārlapaṭṭu) to brahmans.

Remarks
Contains a long eulogy of the kings of the Durjaya family eventually estabiishing their connexion with the Kākatī-yas. In the end are given the names of the Mahāmaṇḍa-jēśvara Kōnakaṇḍravāḍi Bhīmarāja and his two sons Chōḍayarāja and Pōtarāja.
